src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ellipse_sign_119.svg/31px-Ellipse_sign_119.svg.png" decoding="async" width="31" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ellipse_sign_119.svg/47px-Ellipse_sign_119.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ellipse_sign_119.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_119.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>San Germ\xc3\xa1n</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;sa\xc5\x8b<span class="wrap"> </span>xe\xc9\xbe\xcb\x88man&#93;</a></span>) is a historic <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_barrio-pueblo" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> located in the Sabana Grande Valley of southwestern region of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maricao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maricao, Puerto Rico">Maricao</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Lajas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Lajas, Puerto Rico">Lajas</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Hormigueros,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hormigueros, Puerto Rico">Hormigueros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Rojo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cabo Rojo, Puerto Rico">Cabo Rojo</a>, and west of <a href="/wiki/Sabana_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Grande, Puerto Rico">Sabana Grande</a>. San Germ\xc3\xa1n is spread over eighteen barrios plus <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_barrio-pueblo" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n barrio-pueblo">San Germ\xc3\xa1n Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). It is both a principal city of the <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n%E2%80%93Cabo_Rojo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n\xe2\x80\x93Cabo Rojo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Germ\xc3\xa1n\xe2\x80\x93Cabo Rojo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_metropolitan_area#Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez metropolitan area">Mayag\xc3\xbcez\xe2\x80\x93San Germ\xc3\xa1n\xe2\x80\x93Cabo Rojo Combined Statistical Area</a>.\nSan Germ\xc3\xa1n is the second oldest city of Puerto Rico, after <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/Old_town" title="Old town">historic downtown</a> is preserved as the <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Historic_District" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District">San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was, at one time, divided administratively between the San Juan and the San Germ\xc3\xa1n municipalities. The latter covered the western half of Puerto Rico and extended from the western shores of the island to <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a> in the north and <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_in_San_German,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Church_in_San_German%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/250px-Church_in_San_German%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="192" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Church_in_San_German%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/375px-Church_in_San_German%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Church_in_San_German%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/500px-Church_in_San_German%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="524" /></a><figcaption>One of the oldest churches in Puerto Rico.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The population of San Germ\xc3\xa1n when <a href="/wiki/Alonso_Manso" title="Alonso Manso">Alonso Manso</a> was named the first bishop of Puerto Rico in 1511 was "about 50 residents".<sup id="cite_ref-de_Oviedo_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Oviedo-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Outside of San Juan, Puerto Rico, San Germ\xc3\xa1n was one of the largest settlements in the 16th century, as well as <a href="/wiki/Coamo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Coamo, Puerto Rico">Coamo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aguada,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguada, Puerto Rico">Aguada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Spanish settlement in San Germ\xc3\xa1n occurred early in the conquest and <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a> of Puerto Rico. After the destruction of a small early settlement of the same name near modern-day <a href="/wiki/A%C3%B1asco" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xb1asco">A\xc3\xb1asco</a> during a <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> uprising which started in February 1511, in 1512<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the new settlement was built by Miguel D\xc3\xadaz at <a href="/wiki/Guayanilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayanilla">Guayanilla</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nand was named after <a href="/wiki/Germaine_of_Foix" title="Germaine of Foix">Germaine of Foix</a>, the second wife of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">King Fernando II</a>, and in reference of <a href="/wiki/Germanus_of_Auxerre" title="Germanus of Auxerre">Saint Germanus of Auxerre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Floyd_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Floyd-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This town was attacked by <a href="/wiki/French_corsairs" title="French corsairs">French corsairs</a> in August 1528, May 1538 and 1554. The construction of a small fort began in 1540, but work stopped in 1546 when the population of the town began moving inland to the current modern location.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On May 12, 1571, the Royal Audience (<i><a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia" title="Real Audiencia">Real Audiencia</a></i>) of <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> authorized that both the populations of San Germ\xc3\xa1n and <b>Santa Mar\xc3\xada de Guadianilla</b> be merged into a single city due to the constant French attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new city was built on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Marta_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Santa Marta Hills (page does not exist)">Hills of Santa Marta</a>, next to the <a href="/wiki/Guanajibo_River" title="Guanajibo River">Guanajibo River</a> in 1573. Its official name was <b>Nueva Villa de Salamanca</b>, named after the city of Salamanca in Spain. However, the population called the city <b>San Germ\xc3\xa1n el Nuevo</b> (<i>New San Germ\xc3\xa1n</i>) and, eventually, the <b>Villa de San Germ\xc3\xa1n</b> (City of San Germ\xc3\xa1n).\n</p><p>San Germ\xc3\xa1n is also known as the "<i>founder of towns</i>", given the fact that in 1514 the Spanish Crown separated the island into two administrative territories (<i>Partidos</i>). The borders of the two partidos were established as the <a href="/wiki/Camuy_River" title="Camuy River">Camuy River</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Jacaguas_River" title="Jacaguas River">Jacagua River</a> to the south. They were named the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> Partition</i> and the <i>San Germ\xc3\xa1n Partition</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, triggered numerous landslides in San Germ\xc3\xa1n with the significant amount of rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>San Germ\xc3\xa1n is in the southwest region of the island. The town is located on the Sabana Grande valley which is bound by the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> to the north and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Marta_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Santa Marta Hills (page does not exist)">Santa Marta Hills</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lajas_Valley" title="Lajas Valley">Lajas Valley</a> to the south. Mountains in San Germ\xc3\xa1n include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alto_del_Descanso&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alto del Descanso (page does not exist)">Alto del Descanso</a> (2,520&#160;ft; 770&#160;m) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tetas_de_Cerro_Gordo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tetas de Cerro Gordo (page does not exist)">Tetas de Cerro Gordo</a> (2,897&#160;ft; 883&#160;m). San Germ\xc3\xa1n has a number of rivers: <a href="/wiki/Cain_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Cain River">R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xadn</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Duey_(San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Duey (San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Duey</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Rosario" title="R\xc3\xado Rosario">R\xc3\xado Rosario</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guanajibo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guanajibo">R\xc3\xado Guanajibo</a> (Estero), <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Hoconuco" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Hoconuco">R\xc3\xado Hoconuco</a>, Guam\xc3\xa1 River and Rio El Brujo.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1180" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of San Germ\xc3\xa1n.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, San Germ\xc3\xa1n is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 12em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Ancones,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ancones, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Ancones</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%ADn_Alto" title="Ca\xc3\xadn Alto">Ca\xc3\xadn Alto</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%ADn_Bajo" title="Ca\xc3\xadn Bajo">Ca\xc3\xadn Bajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cotu%C3%AD,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cotu\xc3\xad, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Cotu\xc3\xad</a></li>\n<li><a San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Duey Bajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guam%C3%A1,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guam\xc3\xa1, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Guam\xc3\xa1</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hoconuco_Alto" title="Hoconuco Alto">Hoconuco Alto</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hoconuco_Bajo" title="Hoconuco Bajo">Hoconuco Bajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mares%C3%BAa" title="Mares\xc3\xbaa">Mares\xc3\xbaa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minillas,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Minillas, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Minillas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Retiro,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Retiro, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Retiro</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rosario_Alto" title="Rosario Alto">Rosario Alto</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sabana_Eneas" title="Sabana Eneas">Sabana Eneas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sabana_Grande_Abajo" title="Sabana Grande Abajo">Sabana Grande Abajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_barrio-pueblo" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n barrio-pueblo">San Germ\xc3\xa1n barrio-pueblo</a><sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tuna,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Tuna, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">Tuna</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span>  (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in San Germ\xc3\xa1n: Ancones, Comunidad El Retiro, Comunidad Las Quebradas, La Tea, Parcelas Las Carolinas, Parcelas Minillas en Barrio Minillas, Parcelas Sabana Eneas, and Rosario Pe\xc3\xb1\xc3\xb3n.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Climate">Climate</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n<caption>Climate data for San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico (1898-2013)\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="row">Month\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jan\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Feb\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Mar\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Apr\n</th>\n<th mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:San_German_Historic_district.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/San_German_Historic_district.jpg/250px-San_German_Historic_district.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/San_German_Historic_district.jpg/375px-San_German_Historic_district.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/San_German_Historic_district.jpg/500px-San_German_Historic_district.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>Plaza Santo Domingo, located in the <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Historic_District" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District">San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Germ\xc3\xa1n\'s <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Historic_District" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District">historic downtown</a> is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Porta_Coeli_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Porta Coeli (Puerto Rico)"><i>Porta Coeli</i></a> church, one of the earliest Spanish churches built in the Americas. <i>Porta Coeli</i> is still a major historical attraction that attracts both domestic and international tourists every year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg/250px-San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg/375px-San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg/500px-San_Germ%C3%A1n_Auxerre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Plaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza">Plaza</a> Francisco Mariano Qui\xc3\xb1ones and the <a href="/wiki/Church_San_Germ%C3%A1n_de_Auxerre" class="mw-redirect" title="Church San Germ\xc3\xa1n de Auxerre">Church San Germ\xc3\xa1n de Auxerre</a></figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li>Puente de Bolas (Bridge of Balls)</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo Farmacia La Botica</i></span></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo de la Historia de San Germ\xc3\xa1n</i></span> (San Germ\xc3\xa1n history museum)</li>\n<li>Casa Morales</li>\n<li>Ceiba de la Libertad</li>\n<li>San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic Gallery</li>\n<li>Lola Rodr\xc3\xadguez de Ti\xc3\xb3 Museum</li>\n<li>Casa Cruz de la Luna</li>\n<li>Ram\xc3\xadrez de Arrellano y Rossell Museum</li>\n<li>Santo Domingo Plazuela</li>\n<li>Three Races and One Culture Mural</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_Historic_District" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District">San Germ\xc3\xa1n Historic District</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Porta_Coeli_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Porta Coeli (Puerto Rico)">Porta Coeli</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inter-American_University_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter-American University of Puerto Rico">Inter-American University of Puerto Rico</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Church_San_Germ%C3%A1n_de_Auxerre" class="mw-redirect" title="Church San Germ\xc3\xa1n de Auxerre">Church San Germ\xc3\xa1n de Auxerre</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church_Outside_of_Russia" title="Russian Orthodox Church Outside of Russia">Russian Orthodox Church</a> Saint John Climacus (Only Russian Orthodox Church in Puerto Rico)</li></ul>\n<p>The urban center of San Germ\xc3\xa1n is mainly composed of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_architecture" title="Spanish Colonial architecture">Spanish colonial</a> houses. Many have been restored and conserve their Spanish look while other houses are somewhat abandoned and in poor condition. There are ongoing projects employing public and private funding to preserve and restore many houses and monuments and to maintain San Germ\xc3\xa1n\'s colonial era look.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG/250px-SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG/375px-SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG/500px-SanGerman_ParquedeSantoDomingo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a><figcaption>Park in San Germ\xc3\xa1n</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>San Germ\xc3\xa1n celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in late July / early August. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San German Euserre</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in San Germ\xc3\xa1n include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Festival de la Pana \xe2\x80\x93 July</li>\n<li>An\xc3\xb3n Festival \xe2\x80\x93 September</li>\n<li>Christmas Festival \xe2\x80\x93 December</li>\n<li>Christmas Parade \xe2\x80\x93 Early December</li>\n<li>Patron Celebrations (The <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary" title="Our Lady of the Rosary">Virgin of the Rosary</a>)\xe2\x80\x94Celebrated in San Germ\xc3\xa1n\'s Rosario Poblado, which borders the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>San Germ\xc3\xa1n is home to one of Puerto Rico\'s oldest basketball franchises, dating back to the 1930s, the San Germ\xc3\xa1n Athletics (los Atl\xc3\xa9ticos de San Germ\xc3\xa1n), nicknamed "The Orange Monster". Many glories of Puerto Rican basketball have played in San Germ\xc3\xa1n, a city that is also known as "The Cradle of Puerto Rican Basketball". Some of those players are Arquelio Torres, Jos\xc3\xa9 "Picul\xc3\xadn" Ortiz, Eddie Casiano, Nelson Qui\xc3\xb1ones, El\xc3\xadas "Larry" Ayuso, Christian Dalmau, and so many others. Their home court is The Arquelio Torres Ram\xc3\xadrez Court, which houses approximately 5,000 fans.\n</p><p>The Athletic\'s fan base is most commonly referred to as their sixth man, or "The Orange Monster". This is because for a visiting team it\'s extremely hard to win in San Germ\xc3\xa1n due to how vigorous and "into" the game the fans are.\n</p><p>The Athletics have been to 26 National Superior Basketball (BSN) Finals, of which one was cancelled (1953) due to confiscation because of a fight between players from San Germ\xc3\xa1n and the Ponce Lions, giving birth to Puerto Rican basketball\'s most intense rivalry.\n</p><p>Championships (14): 1932, 1936, 1939, 1941, 1942, 1943, 1947, 1948, 1949, 1950, 1985, 1991, 1994, 1997\nSub-Championships (11): 1931, 1933, 1936, 1938, 1940, 1954, 1955, 1956, 1957, 1965, 1986\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The area around San Germ\xc3\xa1n grows fruits (banana, <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapple</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> on mid-scale. <a href="/wiki/Dairy_farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Dairy farms">Dairy farms</a> are also present in small scale. Some locals grow other produce on a small scale.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Business">Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Most businesses are located in or near the downtown area (<a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_barrio-pueblo" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n barrio-pueblo">San Germ\xc3\xa1n Pueblo</a>). <a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_del_Oeste&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plaza del Oeste (page does not exist)">Plaza del Oeste</a> is the main shopping center.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industry">Industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Major employers of the city include Fresenius Kabi, CCL, Wallace International, <a href="/wiki/Baxter_International" title="Baxter International">Baxter Serum Mfg.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cordis_(medical)" title="Cordis (medical)">Cordis</a>, Insertco (print shop for medical instructions inserts), Wallace Silversmiths de Puerto Rico, <a href="/wiki/GE" class="mw-redirect" title="GE">General Electric</a> (production of circuit breakers) and several other companies in the service industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Motion_pictures_filmed_in_San_Germ\xc3\xa1n"><span id="Motion_pictures_filmed_in_San_Germ.C3.A1n"></span>Motion pictures filmed in San Germ\xc3\xa1n</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Motion pictures filmed in San Germ\xc3\xa1n"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Act_of_Valor" title="Act of Valor">Act of Valor</a> (2012) Which follows a Navy Seal squad on a covert mission to recover a kidnapped CIA Agent Morales (<a href="/wiki/Roselyn_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Roselyn S\xc3\xa1nchez">Roselyn S\xc3\xa1nchez</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dinero_Sangre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dinero Sangre (page does not exist)">Dinero Sangre</a> (1986) In a banana republic a ruthless mercenary waits to make a killing in gold. Only two people stand in his way (<a href="/wiki/Guy_Ecker" title="Guy Ecker">Guy Ecker</a>)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span or more races</td>\n<td>727</td>\n<td>2.1%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/200px-Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/400px-Alcald%C3%ADa_de_San_Germ%C3%A1n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a><figcaption>The new City Hall on Luna Street was built in 1989.</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Like all municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, San Germ\xc3\xa1n is administered by a mayor. The current mayor is Virgilio Olivera Olivera from the <a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)">New Progressive Party</a>. Olivera was elected in the 2020 general election.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district IV">Puerto Rico Senatorial district IV</a>, which is represented by two Senators.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>By the 16th century there was a rough road called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Camino de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Camino Real) connecting San Germ\xc3\xa1n (which was located near the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/A%C3%B1asco_River" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xb1asco River">A\xc3\xb1asco River</a>) to other areas of Puerto Rico, including <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Alta, Puerto Rico">Toa Alta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caparra_Archaeological_Site" title="Caparra Archaeological Site">Caparra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, there were 44 bridges in San Germ\xc3\xa1n.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><b>Green</b> \xe2\x80\x93 The Episcopal dignity and also the color of the Shield of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> and his son, don <a href="/wiki/Diego_Col%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Diego Col\xc3\xb3n">Diego Col\xc3\xb3n</a>, Viceroy of the Indies, who named the city in honor of <a href="/wiki/Germaine_of_Foix" title="Germaine of Foix">Germane de Foix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><b>White</b> \xe2\x80\x93 The purity of the blood of the great families who colonized San Germ\xc3\xa1n, according to a history book by <a href="/wiki/Fray_%C3%8D%C3%B1igo_Abbad_y_Lasierra" title="Fray \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra">Fray \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra</a>, a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Benedictines" title="Benedictines">Benedictine</a> monk.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Purple</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Color of the Shield of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">governor of Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><b>First Quarter</b>: The Mitre and the Staff in a green field represent <a href="/wiki/Germanus_of_Auxerre" title="Germanus of Auxerre">St. Germain of Auxerre</a>, the Patron Saint of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Second Quarter</b>: The second quarter exhibits the arms of the Kingdoms of Arag\xc3\xb3n and Sicily, where don Fernando the Catholic reigned.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Third Quarter</b>: In this quarter the arms combine with the County of Foix and the Kingdom of France, which constitute the family shields of <a href="/wiki/Germaine_de_Foix" class="mw-redirect" title="Germaine de Foix">Germaine de Foix</a> whose name is perpetuated as the name of the city of San Germ\xc3\xa1n.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Fourth Quarter</b>: Is Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n\'s shield.\n</p><p><b>The Crown</b>: Is a civic or municipal standard and is used as a stamp for towns and cities; San Germ\xc3\xa1n was assigned five towers to denote that this population formally obtained the title of city from the Spanish crown in the nineteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_34-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The following schools are in San Germ\xc3\xa1n:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li>Bartolome de Las Casas: PK-6</li>\n<li>Georgina Alvarado: PK-5</li>\n<li>Henry W. Longfellow: PK-5</li>\n<li>Herminia C. Ramirez: PK-5</li>\n<li>Julio Victor Guzman: KG-8</li>\n<li>Laura Mercado: 6\xe2\x80\x9312</li>\n<li>Lola Rodriguez de Tio: 9\xe2\x80\x9310</li>\n<li>Mariano Abril: PK-6</li>\n<li>(Second Unit) Francisco Maria Quinones: KG-8</li></ol>\n<p>The main campus of the <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_University_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter-American University of Puerto Rico">Inter-American University of Puerto Rico</a> is located adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n_barrio-pueblo" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n barrio-pueblo">downtown area</a> of San Germ\xc3\xa1n. It was founded in 1912 as the <i>Polytechnical Institute of Puerto Rico</i>, the first <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private university</a> on the island. The <a href="/wiki/Colegio_San_Jos%C3%A9,_San_Germ%C3%A1n,_PR" title="Colegio San Jos\xc3\xa9, San Germ\xc3\xa1n, PR">Colegio San Jos\xc3\xa9</a>, was a private school which was established in San Germ\xc3\xa1n in 1930 and closed in 2017.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Puerto_Ricans_from_San_Germ\xc3\xa1n"><span id="Puerto_Ricans_from_San_Germ.C3.A1n"></span>Puerto Ricans from San Germ\xc3\xa1n</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Puerto Ricans from San Germ\xc3\xa1n"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>PFC <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_recipients_of_the_Distinguished_Service_Cross" title="Puerto Rican recipients of the Distinguished Service Cross">Joseph R. (Jos\xc3\xa9) Mart\xc3\xadnez</a> destroyed a German infantry unit and tank in Tunisia, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, by providing heavy artillery fire, saving his platoon from being attacked in the process. He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Cross_(United_States)" title="Distinguished Service Cross (United States)">Distinguished Service Cross</a>, second only to the <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medal of Honor</a>, by General <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a>, thus becoming the first Puerto Rican recipient of said military decoration.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ubaldino_Ram%C3%ADrez_de_Arellano" title="Ubaldino Ram\xc3\xadrez de Arellano">Ubaldino Ram\xc3\xadrez de Arellano</a>\xe2\x80\x94Senator</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lola_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Ti%C3%B3" title="Lola Rodr\xc3\xadguez de Ti\xc3\xb3">Lola Rodr\xc3\xadguez de Ti\xc3\xb3</a>\xe2\x80\x94poet, author of the original lyrics of Puerto Rico\'s national anthem, <a href="/wiki/La_Borinque%C3%B1a" title="La Borinque\xc3\xb1a">La Borinque\xc3\xb1a</a>, and pro-independence advocate</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benjam%C3%ADn_Marcantoni" title="Benjam\xc3\xadn Marcantoni">Benjam\xc3\xadn Marcantoni</a> \xe2\x80\x93 opera singer</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benicio_del_Toro" title="Benicio del Toro">Benicio del Toro</a>\xe2\x80\x94Award-winning actor</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mariano_Qui%C3%B1ones" title="Francisco Mariano Qui\xc3\xb1ones">Francisco Mariano Qui\xc3\xb1ones</a>\xe2\x80\x94Abolitionist and politician</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_R._Qui%C3%B1ones" title="Samuel R. Qui\xc3\xb1ones">Samuel R. Qui\xc3\xb1ones</a>\xe2\x80\x94Longest-serving President of the Puerto Rico Senate, serving for twenty years.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Gallery">Gallery</h2><span
